TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- kitsuen: smoking tobacco
- tabako: tobacco, cigarette
- inshurinshokkuryouhou: insulin shock therapy
- insurinteikouseishoukougun: insulin-resistance syndrome
- bekutaakouchiku: vector construction

TONE HINT:
- aienka: heavy smoker

Input: kitsuen inshu   tabako   wa   waridasu   ka
Output: /no_think
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- seikou: success, achievement
- sesshokukyoufushou: haphephobia fear of being touched, aphephobia
- manseikoujousen'en: chronic thyroiditis, Hashimoto's disease
- kyuuseisutoresushougai: acute stress disorder, ASD
- bichuukakuwankyokushou: nasal septum deviation, deviated nasal septum

TONE HINT:
- shunkan: moment

Input: shokku   seikou   shibashiba   karada   ga   kyouretsu   hannou   chuukaku   sho   sareta   subete   gusuru   chisai   no   jikan   ni   fuku   shite

```

</details>

### 12. `case-12-chronic-conditions` — History of chronic lung disease (asthma/COPD/pneumonia)

**Input:** `JAP: genzai mata kako ni ikano jyoutai ni natta koto arimasu ka zensoku mansei heisoku haishikkan haien`  
**Direction:** JAP→ENG  
**Preprocessed:** `genzai   mata   kako   ni   shikkan   jou   ni   natta   koto   waridasu   ka   zensoku   mansei   heisoku   kanshikkan   haien`  
**RAG Query Tokens:** `[zensoku, mansei, haien, genzai, kako, jou, heisoku]`

> Have you ever had a sudden onset of asthma, a chronic illness, or a sudden loss of consciousness?

TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").

### 14. `case-14-nausea-black-stool` — Severe symptoms (nausea, fatigue, dizziness, melaena)

**Input:** `JAP: nnnn hakike hidoi no to hirokan dake desu ato yoko ni natte okiagru toki ya tatte suwatte tachi agaru toki ni chotto memai surun desu onaka mo katai kanji shite itsumo i ga itai desu senjyutsu kuroi ben deta desu ga nani ka warui koto da to omoimasu ka`  
**Direction:** JAP→ENG  
**Preprocessed:** `innen   hakike   hidoi   no   to shikkan   dake   desu   ato   yoko   ni   natte   okiagaru   toki   ya   tatte   suwa   tachi   agaru   toki   ni   chotto   memai   tassuru   desu   onaka   mo   katai   kanji   shite   itsumo   i   ga   itai   desu   senshutsu   kuroi   ben   deta   desu   ga   nani   ka   warui   koto   da   to   omoidasu   ka`  
**RAG Query Tokens:** `[hakike, hidoi, ato, yoko, okiagaru, tatsu, tachi, agaru, memai, onaka]`  
#### LLM Output

> I feel nauseous and severe, but I only feel dizzy when I turn to the side or when I stand up or sit up; my stomach also feels uncomfortable, and my legs always hurt. I have had black stools, but I wonder if something is wrong.

**Duration:** 53837ms

> ⭐ **FLIP TRIGGERED** for token `[するん]`!

TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.

- hakike: nausea, feeling like throwing up

### 15. `case-15-follow-up` — Next appointment / Recital context

**Input:** `JAP: wakatta sensei kore ijyou waruknai ranai to iino desu ga sugi no youyaku itsu desuka saisho chichi no hi de hapyoukai aru no de`

<details>
<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- wakaru: to understand, to comprehend
- densenseitankakushou: infectious mononucleosis, mono
- chokoreetonouhou: chocolate cyst, ovarian endometrioma
- koukoresuteroorukesshou: hypercholesterolemia, hypercholesterolaemia
- arukaputonnyoushou: alkaptonuria, alcaptonuria

TONE HINT:
- kudasai: please give me

Input: wakatta   sensei   kore   iryou   wazuka   ranai   to   innou   desu   ga   sugi   no   youyaku   itsu   desuka   saisho   chichi   no   hi   de   happyoukai   aru   no   de
Output: /no_think
```
